NTPC POWER GENERATION PROJECT
WNPC Environmental Action Plan
The Environmental Action Plan
1.l       The LAP has been developed taking Into account the analysis of
NTPC's current performance on environmental and R&R lssues as well as the
analysis carried out by BEI (pare. 3.31) ond NTPC's environmental mangeent
committee. The obiectives of the LAP ares (i) to rationalize and improve
NTPC's organizational structure for environmental management at the corporate
and plant levels; (1i) to improve environmental monitorlng and the preparation
of environmental impact assessments; (iii) to execute a specific program of
remedial environmental measures for NTPC's existing power stations; and
(Lv) to address outstanding R&R issues and to upgrade NTPC"s capability to
prepare and execute R&R programs.
1.2       The EAP can be divided Into four main categoriess (i) Institutional
strengthening; (11) Environmental management and monitoring;
(1ii) Environmental projects and; (iv) Rehabilitation and Resettlement.   The
plan will be implemented largely by NTPC's own personnel. Responsibility for
implementing the ZAP will be of the respective environmental groups namely
EG,, 3MG and CDG at the Corporate Headquarters and plant levels. The progress
of implementation of RAP will be reported to funding agencies by Corporate
Planning. Technical assistance will be provided by consultants in areas like
review of existing environmental policies and standards, training and a number
of specific technical studies to desiga further remedial actions.  The overall
implementation schedule of the ZAP is shown in Appendix 1 and details of
various actions in Appendix 2. Background notes and details of the
implementation schedules are available in the project files.
Main Accomplishments
1.3       The ZAP includes a number of ongoing environmental remedial actions
and the main accomplishment so far achieved are listed belowt
(a) Environmental management documentation has been compiled by NTPCs
corporate headquarters in a more systematic way. It Includes
Ministry of Environment and Forest (MOEP) Clearances and State
Pollution Board Consent Orders for NTPC's power stations as well as
environaAmental information on linked coal mines and associated
transmission lines.
(b)  An Expanded  nitoring Program for air emissions and vastewaters
has been agreed upon with the Bank and is being introduced in all
NTPC's power stations.NTPC bas initiated an Ecological Impacts
Monitoring program based on analysis of satellite ilmgery. The
terms of reference of the studies have been reviewed by the Bank,
and the contract for the first study at Ramga has been
awarded.



- S8 -
lc) NTPC currently has an earth dam safety monitoring program, which
includes regular inspections as well as formal inspection reports.
(d) Experimental trials for ash pond reclamation plantations have been
completed at Singrauli, Ramagundam, Korba and is in progress at
Farakka.
le) Task forces have been assigned to assess remedial measures needed
to upgrade chlorine handling safety, oil itorage spill control
provisions, hazardous materials storage and handling, and to obtain
personnel protective clothing and equipment required for safe
hazardous materials handling.
(f) As the first step in a program of air emissions control equipment
upgrading, electrostatic precipitator (ESP) performance has been
measured in all units at all of the power stations. The ESP
upgrading feasibility studies have been completed. The equipment is
expected to be installed by the third quarter of 1995.
(g) The feasibility studies for a lightweight aggregate manufacturing
plant using fly ash, and a brick manufacturing plant using coal fly
ash are being carried out for installations proposed to be funded
by NTPC at Dadri. The results of these feasibility studies could
also be used for other power stations.
(h) Socio-economic studies have been completed at Farakka (April, 1992)
and Rasmagundam (December, 1992). The socio-economic studies for
the Rihand II and Vindhyachal II were completed in February 1993
and the results are being used for the preparation of the
Resettlement Action Plans for these stations.
Institutional Strengthening
1.4       NTPC has initiated steps during the past year to strengthen the
capabilities to address environmental issues. Broadly, the steps cover two
aspects - organization development and acquisition of expertise to analyze
environmental issues with a view to determine appropriate mitigative measures.
An in-house committee has reviewed the existing capabilities and recomended
for management consideration the future strategic requirements.
1.5       The committee has recommended that the groups responsible for
managing environmental matters within each division (delineated on functional
basis) should be strengthened and made fully functional to achieve their
stated objectives. The three functional groups within the Engineering
Operation and Personnel and Administration Divisions are: (i) Enviromental
Engineering Group responsible for assessing through studies and including
pollution abatement measures in the power projects; (Ui) Environmental
ManAgement Group responsible for monitoring discharge levels of pollutants and
effectiveness of pollution control equipments; (iii) Community Development
Group responsible for R&R and community development activities. Just as in
the case of other functions, for environmental matters too, international
funding agencies will need to call upon the Corporate Planning department who
In turn will coordinate with the functional groups to obtain information or
take up policy matters. The committee has suggested the staffing pattern for
these groups and the persons will be in place at corporate headquarters and at



- 59 -
sites by April 1994. The company has a system of periodic review meetings in
project implementation and operation functions. Such meetings have helped the
site General Hanagers in planning and for achieving targets and the Committee
has recommended to extend the system to environmental matters. The
recommended to extend the system to environmental matters. The environmental
review meetings will be chaired by regional Executive Directors on a quarterly
basis. The first such meeting for each of the four regions will be held by
June 1993.
1.6       Persons will be reassigned to the environmental groups from other
functional areas of the company. The necessary expertise will be built up
through in-house training program, association with consultants and exposure
to international practices.
1.7       NPTC already has a twinning arrangement with British Electricity
International Ltd. (BII) United Kingdom and experts from National Power have
visited the NTPC facilities to access their needs. Under this arrangement
National Power will assist NTPC in (a) conducting environmental appraisal,
(b) developing guidelines for environmental management, (c) examining current
laboratory and monitoring practices and recommending additional requirements.
1.8       The 1-7, a group of internationally reputed utilities have been
sounded during the course of appraisal of this loan proposal and they have
expressed interest in assisting NTPC in environmental related studies. The
assistance will be by way of grant for man-months time of their experts and
cover the cost of visits of NTPC personnel to their facilities.  Experts from
these major utilities would be well versed with international practices.
governmental regulations and would have a pragmatic view on environmental
matters concerning large coal based power projects. Under this program,
NTPC's expertise will be developed in (a) developing overall targets for
pollution and waste reduction (including energy conservation), (b) development
and engineering of effluent treatment and emission control systems,
(c) operations from environmental view point and utilizing of ash;
(d) establishing computer center and data bank for atmospheric emission
dispersion models, effluent discharge data collection and analysis: and (e)
strengthening of human resources by way of training of management and
operational at E-7 facilities to fully appreciate the current international
environment management practices.
Eavironmental mana_ement and monitorina
1.9        This component focusses on: (i) developing NTPC's environmental
policies; (ii) standardizing effluent and emissions disposal and treatment
technologies; (iii) establishment of additional company training programs to
keep pace with changing environmental regulations, for persons at various
management and operations levels, for environment and safety; (iv) central
follow-up and control on environmental compliance and safety performance of
plants; (v) enhancing monitoring data collection and analysis capability and
(vi) carrying out of enviromental audits.
Environmental Proiects
1.10      This component includes: (i) ash management; (ii) ash slurry water
recycling; (iii) feasibility of ash backfill at abandoned or operating coal
mines; (iv) ash pond reclamation; tv) ash leachate analysis and groundwater



- 60 -
contamination monitoring; (vi) electrostatic precipitator upgrade program;
(vii) retrofitting of closed cycle condenser cooling systems; (viii) chlorine
handling safety improvements; (is) upgrade spill containment provisions for
bulk fuel oil storage; (x) upgrade hazardous material storage; (xi) solid
waste management and (zii) sanitary vastevater projects.
Resettlement and Rehabilitation
1.11        This component includess
(a) Implementation of NTPC's R&R policy. Special attention will be
given to ensure income restoration and to improve the consultative
process with the PAPs;
(b) Establish andlor strengthen R&R units at the corporate and plant
levels to adequately cover all aspects of land acquisition,
community development, as well as planning, implementation and
monitoring of R&R programs;
(c) Develop a human resource development program of personnel involved
in R&R; and
(d) Complete the remaining infrastructure facilities for PAFs of
Singrauli in accordance with agreed schedule. [Other remaining
actions related to the implementation of ongoing R&R programs such
as Talcher, Farakka etc. have not been specifically included in the
ZAP.]
(e) Carry-out or complete socio-economic studies for existing projects
Singrauli, RiBhand I, Vindhyachal I, Korba (on-going) to ascertain
the present economic status of the PAls and develop community
facilities action plans in coordination and consultation with local
government and PAls.
Implementation
1.12        Proposals for providing the technical assistance and training
required by N7PC are currently under consideration with the recently formed
'E7 Network"" and, the terms of reference is placed at Appendix 3.
Cost Estimates
1.13      Investments re4uired for the implementation of remedial measures
(to be financed from the proceeds of the proposed loan) and cost of technical
assistance and training are placed at Appendiz 4.

in April 1992 to provide assistance to developing countries to inter alia
develop environmentally acceptable energy supplies.

ANNEX 3.2
Appendix 2
NTPC: ENVIRONMENTAL ACTION PLAN
Summary Description of Tasks
Institutional Strengthening
1.1       Based on the recommendations of the in-house committee, NTPC plans
to strengthen the organizational framework for dealing with environment
related matters. Additional staff will be reassigned to the various
environmental groups at corporate headquarters and sites. A further review of
the efficacy of the organization will be taken up by the in-house committee
after a two year period. Quarterly review meetings will be held at regional
level.
1.2       The persons assigned to environmental groups will be suitably
trained through in-house and other training programs and wide exposure to
current international practices.
1.3       Under the existing twinning arrangement with BEI the capabilities
of the persons will be enhanced to accomplish environmental appraisal
formulate guidelines for environmental management and upgrade current
laboratory and monitor1lg practices.
1.4       The L-7 group will be approached to provide technical assistance
for specific studies which may include development of overall targets for
pollution and waste reduction; development and engineering of effluent
treatment and emission control systems; operations from environmental view-
point; ash utilization; establishment of computer center and data bank for
atmospheric dispersion models, effluent discharge data collection and
analysis; strengthening of HRD).
Environmental Manasement and Monitoring
1.5       Apart from determining environmental policies, environmental
management activities include the compilation and regular updating of
environmental documentation, such as environmental clearances and consent
orders from G.O.I. and State regulatory authorities for NTPC facilities as
well as associated coal mines and transmission lines. Recent new GOI
regulations require that corporate environmental audits are to be included in
NTPC's annual reports, starting from the fiscal year ending March 1993.
1.6       All NTPC power stations store hazardous materials over the
threshold quantities specified in recently amended environmental regulations
and NTPC must develop Disaster Management Plans for each of it's facilities,
in cooperation with the State Pollution Control Boards, and local disaster
relief agencies, including hospitals. Under the RAP, NTPC has worked out a
schedule to bring each facilities plant in compliance with the new
regulations. Similarly, all industrial facilities, such as NTPC power
stations, are now required to obtain liability insurance to cover damages
resultiag from hazardous materials spills or other environmental damages. The
liability cap is set at Re 500 million. State Pollution Control Boards are
Includin this requirement In Consent Order renewals.



- 68 -
1.7       General Environmental Monitoring.  NTPC. in consultation with the
Bank has agreed to expand their environmental monitoring program to include a
broader spectrum of parameters (See Appendix 2). The expanded environmental
monitoring program will allow for identification of any problem pollution
sources, and quantitative diagnostlc evaluation of the severity of the problem
and possible remedial actions. All NTPC power plants have the environmental
laboratory equipment needed to perform the regular analyses included in the
EAP, except in Korba. An atomic absorption spectrophotometer is required in
the environmental laboratory at the Rorba power station and this will be
installed as part of the EAP.
1.8                                     . A program for monitorlng ecological
impacts in the area surrounding the NTPC power plants has been included in the
EAP. The Terms of Reference for studies at all of the power stations have
been agreed with the Bank. Remote sensing data collected from satellite
observation will be used to track changes in terrestrial ecology over time.
Changes in vegetation patterns, crop densities, and land use would be
documented in the studies. The studies include ground truth surveys and field
experiments, in order to develop proper interpretation techniques for
satellite imagery, and to compliment study findings. Satellite imagery from
three different periods at each power station will be examined: (i) pre-
construction. to establish baseline data; (ii) post construction to cover
impacts of construction, and; (iii) current conditions, to cover impacts of
power plant operations. A contract for such a study at the Ramsgundam power
station has been awarded. Requirements for remedial measures, should negative
impacts be observed, will be discussed with the Bank. The RAP includes
schedules for initiation and completion of all the above studies, as well as
implementation of remedial actions.
1.9       Earth Dam Safety Monitoring. NTPC has a program of regular visual
inspections of earth dams by qualified engineers of the ash pond dikes, with
formal inspection reports. The earth dam safety monitoring program under the
ZAP includes installation of monitoring instruments. These instruments would
also monitor lateral movement of the dam, and peizometers to measure the
seepage surface within the dam.
1.10      Power Plant Community and Occupational Health Monitoring.
Community health surveys, with baseline data collected prior to plant start-up
are MOEF. G.O.I. has also occupational being specified by MOEP in some recent
clearances exposure standards applicable to power plants. The RAP includes an
occupational exposure and health monitoring program. The program will be
initiated by an assessment of equipment and personnel requirements.
1.11      Mercury Fate and Transport Study.  The EdF study of the Singrauli
area (location of NTPC power stations Rihand and Vindhyachal), revealed
mercury, a bio-accumulative heavy metal, in the Rihand reservoir sediments,
fish, and food crops; in some cases above levels of concern. Anthropogenic
sources of mercury in the area include a mercury chlor-alkali plant (Kanoria
chemicals), coal fired power plants, and possibly the coal mines. The ZAP
includess (i) an investigation into the potential origins (coal mines),
environmental transport and environmental fate of mercury. Undisturbed core
samples would be taken in the coal deposits and overburden, and analyzed for
micro-constituents, including mercury. Mercury is a volatile metal, which may
be concentrated in the overburden or in the coal itself. These undisturbed
samples would be compared to the coal as delivered to the power plants; (Li) a



. 69 -
mercury fate and transport study, to determine the partitioning of mercury
through the thermal power generation process and pollution control equipment,
and; (iii) mercury contamination monitoring. This study would address the
environmental partitioning of mercury releases. It would include environmental
sampling and human exposure monitoring. Remedial actions, if required will be
implemented as part of the EAP.
Environmental Proiects
1.12      Environmental projects consist of retro-fitting and construction of
pollution control facilities at power plants, mainly related to ash management
and disposal, electrostatic precipitator upgrades, and hazardous materials
management.
1.13      Ash Management.  Ash management projects include utilization for
lightweight cement aggregate and brick-making, and construction of these
facilities, as well as modification of the ash management system at the power
plant to facilitate utilization, that is, construction of dry ash disposal
provisions. NTPC has performed the feasibility studies and proposes to build
lightweight aggregate and brick making facilities at Dadri. These facilities
are scheduled for completion by 1994.
1.14      Ash Slurry Water Recycling.  Great quantities of water are used at
the power plants to slurry the coal ash for disposal via pipeline to the ash
ponds. The ZAP includes a program for changing ash disposal systems at all of
the power plants from once-through systems with disposal of effluent, to
recycling systems where the ash slurry water is recycled. In the ash slurry
water recycling system only the blow-down is discharged after treatment. Ash
slurry recycling has been a stipulated in some of the recent MOE? clearances,
and is part of G.O.I.'s efforts to upgrade power plants to 'zero environment
discharge" facilities, that is zero discharge of environmental contaminants.
The ash slurry recycling system would also conserve fresh water supplies.
Contracts for construction of the ash recycling system at Ramagundam have been
awarded in the last quarter of 1992 and construction will be completed in
1994. The ash handling system at Talcher is being constructed as a recycling
system. Ash slurry water recirculation system will be constructed as advised
by the respective State Pollution Control Board at the existing stations.
1.15      Ash Backfill at Coal Mines.  The ZAP includes studies for the
feasibility backfilling ash in operating mines in the proximity of the power
plants. Discussions with Coal India are underway. An appropriate mining
technology will have to be adopted in mining operations by the coal companies
in order to facilitate ash backfilling.
1.16      Ash Pond Reclamation.  Ash pond reclamation can commence on site
when *cells' or areas of the ash pond are filled to their ultimate levels.
Procurement or growth of the massive numbers of plant materials needed should
begin two years in advance of the planned reclamation effort. Experimental ash
pond plantation trials have been performed at Singrauli, Ramagundam, Xorba,
and Farakka (in progress) with good results. Several commercially valuable
species have been successfully grown using the coal ash as growth media. One
of the most encouraging achievements has been the growth of a specLes used by
silkworms, as well as the silkworms themselves. This accomplishment points to
the possibility of returning the ash pond areas to commercial use for oustees,
if ash pond reclamation and rehabilitation planning are carefully coordinated.



- 70 -
Ramagundam, Parakka and Vindhyachal ash ponds have a minimum life of another
15 years and so reclamation plans are not included in the RAP.
1.17      Ash Leachate Analysis and Groundwater Contamination Monitoring.
Coal contains trace quantities of heavy metals, which can become environmental
contaminants when huge quantities of coal are burned in the thermal generation
of electrical power. Contaminants will partition between stack emissions,
bottom ash and fly ash. Large quantities of water are used to slurry the ash
and move it to the ash disposal ponds. Leachate from the ash disposal ponds
has the potential to contaminate groundwater. Groundwater monitoring
requirements are included in NTPC's recent MOEF clearances. The first phase
of the EAP covers ash leachate analysis, in order to characterize potential
leachate contaminants. The groundwater protection program includes hydrologic
studies at the new ash pond sites and design of adequate leachate containment
measures, and groundwater monitoring at existing ash ponds, with remedial
response measures as necessary.
1.18      Electrostatic Precipitator Upgrade Program.  Remedial measures have
already been initiated to improve the efficiency of the air pollution control
equipment (electrostatic precipitators) at several of the plants. These
facilities were built prior to the promulgation of current, more stringent
emission control standards. In some cases the new standards exceed the
designed air quality specifications of the original equipment by over four
hundred percent. The electrostatic precipitator upgrading program was already
underway prior to the preparation of the EAP in as much as ESP performance
evaluations had been undertaken. Design modification feasibility studies have
been made by NTPC. Electrostatic field plates will be installed in the
Idum=yW fields of several ESP units, while others will have new microprocessor
controls installed, or both. The work for all NTPC's power plants is
scheduled for completion by the end of the first quarter of 1995. Part of the
Bank loan may be used the finance the ESP equipment.
1.19      Closed Cycle Condenser Cooling Systems.  MOEF is presently
reviewing the standards for permissible temperature rise for hot water
discharges. The results are expected by November 1993 and NTPC will implement
the measures to comply with these requirements thereafter. NTPC will proceed
according to existfing regulations In any case by November 1994. (Vindhyachal
was designed and constructed with a closed cycle condenser cooling system, and
a closed system will be used in the next phase of expansion). Discharge of
heated effluent is not environmentally acceptable under most circumstances,
nor is the once through system as efficient as a closed system where surface
vater ambient temperatures are as high as those found in India.
1.20      Chlorine Handlin8 Safety Improvements. Chlorine is handled at each
facility in one ton containers. Between 12 and 24 one-ton containers normally
located at each power plant site. A spill from a one ton cylinder of chlorine
can create a lethal toxic gas cloud for as many as five miles downwind. NTPC
has assigned a task force to assess the chlorine handling safety issues at
each facility. The ZAP includes provision for remedial measures (such as
installation of automatic leak alarm systems), for safer chlorine handling, as
well as a program for obtaining personnel protective equipment and leak
steaming gear.
1.21      Upgrade Spill Containment Provisions for Bulk Fuel Oil Storage.



- 71 -
Bulk fuel oil is stored in cylindrical steel tanks in all of the facilities
surveyed. These tanks are surrounded by dikes; however, the rainwater drains
either cannot be closed or are customarily left open, comprodisin3 the
containment integrity of the dike system. A task force has been assigned to
assess upgrades needed for spill control at the oil storage areas. The EAP
includes a schedule for the implementation of remedial measures.
1.22      Upsrade Hazardous Materials Storage.  In all of the NTPC facilities
surveyed during the supervisory mission, acid and caustic bulk storage tanks
were located within diked areas or on pads surrounded by drainage trenches;
however, the drainage trenches lead directly to the neutralizing pits, which
are full of water. Should a massive spill of concentrated acid or caustic
occur, there is no way to stem the flow before it reaches the neutralization
tank. A violent exothermic reaction would occur should this happen, putting
human life and limb in jeopardy. A task force has been assigned to assess
remedial measures needed at the hazardous materials storage and handling
areas, and the RAP includes provLsions for implementation of remedial
measures. The task force will also address the needs for personnel protective
equipment.
1.23      Solid Waste Management.  UTPC will generate solid waste management
plans for each of the power generating facilities under the UAP. These solid
waste streams include clarifier sludge from raw water treatment, and solid
waste generated in the township. NTPC is assessing the solid waster
management practices at its stations and will finance and implement an
environmental compatible plan for solid waste.
1.24      Sanitary Wastewater Proiects.  In light of the endemic waterborne
disease problem in India, the NTPC facilities should be equipped with
functional sanitary wastewater treatment facilities, manned with competent
trained operators, and maintained so as to remain functional. Sanitary
vastewater treatment upgrade and/or repair projects are Included in the ZAP
for Riband, Kamagundam, Parakka, and Xorba.



- 72 -
ANNEX 3.2
Appendix 3
NTPC POWER GENERATION PROJECT
TECHNICAL ASSISTANCE FOR ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT
Terms of Reference
1.1       The technical assistance for institutional strengthening of the
technical and social environment capabilities of NTPC will includes (a)
development of policies and regulations:
(b)  establishment of corporate standards in operations, development and
engineering in respect of environmental aspects, safety.
monitoring. auditing and EIAs, infrastructure for rehabilitation
colonies, and R'R budgeting and norms;
(c)  organization of laboratory;
(d)  human resources development; and
(e)  data management improvement.  Additional activities would involve
the regional and plant site levels. Under the technical assistance
for R&R, creating mechanisms for encouraging innovation in R&R and
community development, better sociological capability, and
refinement of existing policy would be broad objectives.
Current Environmental Organization
Technicals
1.2       Corporate Environmental Management Structure.  Environmental impact
assessment and field investigations currently come under different Directors.
Carrying out environmental impact assessment is the responsibility of the
Engineering Services Division and reports to the Director of Technical.
Environmental monitoring, and the field investigations involved in development
of environmental impact assessments, come under a different Director, the
Director of operations Division. Ash utilization programs also fall under the
Director of Operations Division. Resettlement and rehabilitation, as well as
reforestation fall under the Director of Personnel and Administration
Department.
1.3       Environmental Impact Assessment. NTPC currently employs 12 persons
in the corporate Environmental engineering Group (EEG). The disciplines
covered by the staff include all of those needed to produce EIAs, including a
qualified sociologist at corporate headquarters to handle the resettlement and
rehabilitation (R&R) aspects of EIAs, who is temporarily posted in the
Southern Region office to oversee socio-economic studies for southern region
projects.
1.4       Corporate Overview of Environmental Management.  Compliance with
environmental regulations and environmental management has been the
responsibility of the General Manager of each power plant. NTPC established
an Environment Management Group at Corporate Center under the Director of



- 73 -
Operations (in November, 1991) with basic objectives of (a) coordination with
stations, Engineering division on all environmental matters, (b) to carry out
trend analysis of pollution monitoring data and prepare exception reports,
(c) providing operational feedback to engineering for carrying out necessary
modifications in existing/future system, and (d) providing corporate support
to the stations.
1.5       Environmental Management at Power Plants.  Each NTPC power station
has an independent 'Environmental Management Group' headed by a Senior
Manager. this Senior Manager reports to the facility General Manager and also
provides information/exception reports to Environmental Management Group at
Corporate Center. The basis objectives of the Environmental Management Group
at each site is (a) coordination with State Pollution control Boards,
(b) pollution monitoring, and (c) data analysis, corrective measures and
exception reporting.
1.6       Resettlement and Rehabilitation (R&R).  At Corporate level, the
responsibility of collection and collation of various statistics on R&R
measures taken by NTPC projects and providing these statistics to various
agencies is under the purview of Personnel and Administration (P&A). The land
acquisition and implementation of R&R policies of Company is the
responsibility of site P&A.
1.7       Objectives of NTPC.  NTPC has recently reformulated the
responsibilities for the Environmental Engineering Groups (a) associating in
site selection for new projects with engineering services; (b) EIA studies for
new project sites and obtaining clearances; (c) finalization of specification
of equipments for pollution monitoring; (d) special studies relating
environmental problemst (e) interaction with MOEF, Pollution Control Boards
and funding agencies for new projects; and (f) provide assistance to sites in
overcoming specific technical problems related to environment.
1.8       The scope of the Environmental Management Group includes:
(a) coordination and monitoring with stations, regions, CC engineering
Division and other concerned agencies on all environmental matters concerning
operating stations; (b) to carry out trend analysis of pollution monitoring
data and prepare exception reports; (c) environmental audit of power stations;
td) providing operational feedback to Engineering for carrying out necessary
modifications in existing/future systems, overseeing implementation of
modification/ improvement programs; and (e) providing corporate support to
stations.
1.9       The scope of Resettlement and Rehabilitation (R&R) group includess
(a) socio-economic studies, (b) EIA in respect of R&Rs finalization of R&R
plans for new projects, and (c) various R&R measures: policy review and
ensuring implementation.
1.10      Proposed Objective of Technical Assistances  the objectives of the
Technical Assistance team will be to assist NTPC in achieving their states
goals for environmental management.



_74 -
(a)  overall Obiective:  enhance computer data bases, environmental
modelling capabilities, CIS mapping capabilities and office
technology for the environmental groups;
(b)  Technical Objectives:  (i) standardize effluent and emissions
disposal and treatment technologies, ash water recirculation and
ash utilization, (ii) establish additional company training
programs, to keep pace with changing environmental regulations for
workers at various management and operational levels for
environment and safety, and (iii) enhance monitoring data
collection and analysis capability.
(c)  Resettlement and Rehabilitation Obiectivess  (i) strengthen the
human resources development program, and (ii) improve quality of
life in employee's colonies.
1.11      Technical Activities.  The Technical Assistance team will assist in
the following activities being carried out by the Corporate Environmental
Engineering and Environmental Management Groups.
(a) Regulations:
gi) formulate operational guidelines to conform with 601's
environmental standards, laws and regulations;
(ii) develop overall corporate targets for pollution and waste
reduction; these may cover more areas than government
regulations andlor be more stringent than current regulations;
and
(iii)  develop energy conservation programs for the generation,
transmission and utilization of electric power.
(b) Establish Corporate Standards:
(i) Operationst
a. fuel quality standards and a policy for fuel selection;
b. operations methods to minimize emissions and effluents; and
c. utilization of ash
(ii) Development and Engineerings
a. long term environmental planning and action plans;
b. environmental equipment selection;
c. determination of effluent and emissions treatment systems;
d. engineering safety standards; and
e. directives and guidelines for preparation of environmental
impact assessments.
(iii) Safety:
a. safety rating system; and
b. emergency contingency plans and drills



- 75 -
(iv) Monitoring - Develop Standards and Guidelines fors
a.  monitoring methods, frequency, analysis, and data
reporting;
b.  equipment selection; and
c.  establish a computer center and data bank for atmospheric
emissions dispersion models, and monitoring data collection
and analysis.
(v) Corporate environmental laboratory:
a. the Environmental Management and environmental impact
assessment groups should be supported with adequate field
mobilization, sampling and analysis equipment.
(vi) Facilitation of environmental initiatives in laboratory and
field studies.
(vii) Training centers for management and operations personnel in
environmental and occupational health and safety management and
policy.
1.12      Resettlement and Rehabilitation Activities.  The Resettlement and
Rehabilitation unit will be established to take care of all aspects arising
out of land acquisition, community development, planning, implementation and
monitoring.
1.13      The Technical Assistance team will assist in the following
activities being done by the Corporate R&R Groups
(a) strengthen the human resources development program;
(b) set up awards for staff at all levels, and for individual power
plants, foe excellence in the R&R and community development field.
1.14      At the plant site, the R&R units will be assisted in carrying out
the following:
(a) broaden the concept of R&R to include community development in the
vininity of the plant and establish local NGO's which represent
NTPC staff and family members and other local interest groups; and
(b)  improve quality of life in employee's colonies.
1.15      Support Services Activities Corporate Level for R&R and Technical.
Technical Assistance team shall assist to develop the following support
services at the corporate level.
1.16      Develop human resources by establishing a clearly defined career
development program with professional growth opportunities.
1.17      Development data management services to:
(a)  support environmental monitoring and monitoring data analysis;



- 76 -
(b)  design monitoring dat. analysis softwaret
(c) develop geographic information database to support environmental
assessments;
(4) develop or obtain software for environmental impact analysis to
support environmental assessments; and
(e) word processing and report production equipment and staff to
support all operations under the head of the Environmental
Department, Environment.
1.18      Implementation.  The objectives and the activities of the Technical
Assistance are given above. These need to be discussed between the
consultants and NTPC for deciding the implementation schedule. NTPC shall
make available to the consultants the existing practices being adopted in the
areas of activities and the consultants can assess the quantum of work
involved in bringing about the improvements to achieve the levels of
international practices.
1.19      Areas of Expertise and Manpower Requirements. The Technical
Assistance Team need to include expertise in the following areas:
(a) environmental management, (b) environmental regulatory programs,
(c) sociology, resettlement and rehabilitation, (d) computerized data
management, (e) professional development programs, and (f) implementation of
ash management including utilization of ash etc. A total effort of about
fifty man-months would be required for all the activities. The experts for
specific assignments under this program need to be identified in consultation
with NTPC. NTPC will be given their biodata in advance and NTPC's consent
will be required for their assignment.

Page 1 of 6
INDIA
NTPC POWER GENERATION PROJECT
1.1       This annex includes a copy of the background note on NTPC's
environmental problems which was distributed to the Board on April 14. 1993
together with the Environmental Assessment Summaries (EAS) for ULhand II and
Vindhyachal 1I as well as a brief summary of each EAS.
Environmental Assessments
1.2       The first two projects to be included under the proposed time-slice
project (Rihand IT M2U500MW) and Vindhyachal IT (2Z500MW) power stations in
the Siugrauli area) have each been subject to a full Category A environmental
assessment and the Environmental Assessment sumnaries prepared by NTPC are
attached as Annex 1 and 2. The proposed NTPC power stations and the Dudhichua
Coal Mine (Stage TI) of the Northern Coalfields Ltd. (NCL), from which the
power stations will be initially supplied, have obtained environmental
clearances from the Ministry of Environment and Forest (MOEP). NCL has
submitted quarterly progress reports to NOEP on the status of the
Environmental Management Plans (IMPs) for Amlori, Nigahi and Dudhichua mines,
which supply the existing NTPC power stations in the Singrauli area. GOI has
been requested to provide the Bank with NOEP's assessment of NCL's
implementation of the EMPs prior to negotiations.
1.3       Agreement has been reached with NTPC that for all subsequent Bank
financed power plants under the project, category A environmental assessments
would be completed and reviewed with the Bank before issuance of tender
documents for Bank financed procurement packages.
Environmental Action Plan
1.4       During project preparation a detailed assessment was made of NTPC's
environmental performance. Most of NTPC's existing power plants were designed
and built at a time when environmental standards were less stringent.
Therefore, NTPC's power stations do not operate at today's 00I environmental
standards, but a program to upgrade the environmental performance of its
existing stations is already in place. Rihand II and Vindhyachal II are being
designed to meet GOI standards. These designs are compatible with World Bank
standards. Annex 3 describes the pertinent COX and World Bank standards. The
same approach will be followed for other Bank financed power plants. Other
power plants in NTPC's investment program will be designed to meet GOI
standards.
1.5       To make the operation of NTPC's existing plants and the design of
its new power plants environmentally more sustainable, a comprehensive
Environmental Action Plan (SAP) has been prepared by NTPC, in consultation
with the Bank. The SAP covers all NTPC operations and addresses the required
institutional strengthening of NTPC to deal effectively with environmental and
R&R problems. It includes the investments required to implement remedial
actions to enable existing plants to meet the latest GO0 environmental
standards. A sumhary of the draft SAP is attached as Annex 4. The EAP will
be finalized during negotiations and satisfactory implementation of the ZAP
will be a condition of the loan.



- 91 -
Annex 3.8
Page 2 of 6
NTPC's Resettlement and Rehabilitation Policy
1.6       NTPC operates in several states and to ensure a common approach, it
has formulated in 1992 its own comprehensive rehabilitation and resettlement
(R&R) policy for project affected families, which was approved by the Ministry
of Power (Annex 5). The basic objective of the policy is to ensure that after
a reasonable transition period, the affected families regain, if not improve,
their previous standard of living. A number of options like 'land for land',
training to upgrade skills, allotment of sbops with seed money as loan, self-
employment with seed money as grant, jobs with NTPC in the unskilled and
semiskilled categories are included In the policy.
1.7       NTPC's R&R policy needs to be strengthened to provide that the
,land for land' option is available not only through the application of the
land acquisition act, but also on a willing buyeriseller basis through a land
purchase committee. Adoption of a R&R policy by NTPC acceptable to the Bank
will be a condition of negotiations.
1.8       As concerns NTPC's existing stations, the YAP includes socio-
economic studies to ascertain the present economic status of project affected
families (PAFs) and provides, where found to be needed, for the funding and
implementation of community development programs, including necessary income
restoration measures. The RAP would reinforce the ongoing efforts under
existing Bank projects, Second Farakka Thermal Power project (Ln. 2442-IN,
1984) and Talcher Power project (Ln. 2895-IN, 1987).
1.9       NTPC has prepared Resettlement Action Plans (RAPs) for Rihand II
(67 PAPs) and Vindhyachal II (77 PAPs) and they are currently being discussed
with the project affected famLlies (PAFs) and the local authorities. RAPs
acceptable to the Bank will be finalized during appraisal and endorsement by
the relevant State authorities will be a condition for Board presentation.
The 87 PArs of the Stage IT of the Dudhichua Coal Mine are being resettled in
accordance with the integrated Environmental Management Plan (EMP) for the NCL
coal fields approved by MOEF in 1987.
1.10      For subsequent power plants to be financed by the Bank under the
project, the preparation of a Resettlement Action Plan satisfactory to the
Bank and endorsed by the State authorities would be a condition of
disbursement of Bank funds.
Sustainable Environmental Development in the Singrauli area
1.11      During implementation of earlier Bank financed projects in the
Singrauli area (Singrauli I, Cr. 685-IN, 1977 and Singrauli II, Cr.1027-IN,
1980 and Dudhichua Stage I, Ln. 2393-IN, 1984), it was recognized that
remedial actions were required to adequately address the increasing
environmental and socio-economic problems in that region. A major study by
Electricitd de France (Edt) and Groupe Charbonnages de France, entitled
'Environmental Study of the Singrauli Area', financed under the Second
Singrauli Power Project of NTPC was completed in 1991. Several follow up
studies on: air pollution from thermal power plants; industrial pollution
control for specific industries in the area, reclamation and reforestation of



- 918
Annex 3.8
Page 3 of 6
the coal mining areas, general area reforestation and watershed protection,
urban relocation and rehabilitation and institutional and administrative
options for the Singrauli region, which were financed from Japanese grant
funds and executed by the Bank, were completed during the course of 1992. In
addition, a Regional Development Plan has been prepared by the Town and
Country Planning Organization of GOI.
1.12       In May 1992, the BSank submitted to GO  a reports Idat.
Sustainable Develoimet in the Sinhrauli Realn - Towards An Action Plan.  The
executive susnmary of the report is attached as Annex 6. In J.une 1992, GOI
appointed a Steering Committee on Singrauli, chaired by the Ministry of Urban
Development comprising representatives of central and state agencies involved
in the region. In accordance with the recommendations contained in the report
NTPC and NCL have drawn up their respective action plans for sustainable
development in the Singrauli region. NTPC's environmental remedial actions
have been incorporated in the ZAP and the Action Plan for Sustainable
Development in the Singrauli Region for the Coal Sector prepared by NCL is
attached as Annex 7.
1.13      GoI has been asked to provide a formal response to the Bank's
report on Sustainable Development in the Singrauli Region for discussion
during negotiations.
Consultative Processes
1.14      Several rounds of public consultation have taken place during the
preparation of the project. A presentation of the final report of the EdF
study for the Singrauli area was held in Kay 1992 and attended by
representatives of MOEP, members of the Pollution Control Boards, concerned
ministries of 0OI, industries in the Singrauli area and NG10. A public
consultatioa meeting was held at Singrauli in July 1992, to inform the local
populatior. and organizations of the proposed Rihand II and Vindhyachal II
power stations and the proposed RAPs. A detailed socio-economic survey was
completed by NTPC and the process of consultation of the PAFs cm the R&R
options started in February 1993. Local NG00 will be involved in the
community development activities sponsored by WMPC.
Summary of the EAS for Rihand II
1.15      The NTPC project will add an additional 1,000 MK  generating
capacity as Stage II of the kihand Superthermal Power Project (RhSTPP).
RhSTPP is located on the banks of the large man-made reservoir Gobind Ballabh
Pant Sagar (GBPS) in the state of Uttar Pradesh (UP). The project components
include the power generation facility, the associated coal mines and power
transmission system. All environmental clearances have been obtained, with
the exception of one segment of power transmission line.
1.16      Site and Surroundint: The reservoir was constructed for use in
power generation in the 1960s, and since then the area has undergone large
scale Industrialization, with exploitation of a large coal deposit,
development of coal fired power plants, several chemical Industries, and a
cement factory located about 30 kilometers to the north.



- 92 -
Annex S.8
Page 4 of 6
1.17      Project History. Land Acauisition and Resettlements  Due to land
acquisition, 1215 families were affected and 678 families displaced. NTPC
initiated rehabilitation measures for the affected families, and most have
moved into permanent housing. NTPC initiated community development activities.
A detailed socioeconomic study to ascertain present economic status vill be
undertaken as part of NTPC's Environmental Action Plan. In the Dudhichua Stage
I Mine development 63 families have been resettled and rehabilitated. NCL
also initiated community development activities.   Bank supervision missions
have confirmed that there are no outstanding R&R issues with respect to the
Stage I mining development.
1.18      Environmental Baseline Data:  Studies have revealed contamination
of the reservoir, it's sediments, fish and local food crops. Contaminants
include heavy metals, pesticides and other toxic chemicals. The reservoir
exhibits thermal stratification and blue-green algae blooms, which exacerbate
dissolved oxygen depletion in the lower strata. Air quality in the area is
generally good, with the exception of wind blown dust.
1.19      Rihand Stane II Environmental Controls: Psrticulate emissions from
the stacks will be controlled through high efficiency electrostatic
precipitators.
The units will be designed for 100 milligrams per cubic meter particulate
emissions from the stacks after controls. A tall stack height (275 meters)
will be used to achieve wider dispersal of stack emissions including oxides of
sulfur and nitrogen. In addition, as per stipulation of the environmental
clearance, provision of space will be made for retrofitting flue gas
desulfurization.  A closed-cycle cooling system will be used for condenser
cooling with treatment of blow-down prior to discharge. The ash generated
from both Stage I and Stage II would be pumped to an ash pond in slurry form
and the slurry water recycled. Blow-down from the ash pond slurry water
recycling system would be treated prior to discharge. The ash pond itself will
be lined to prevent groundwater contamination. Provision for collection of dry
fly ash will also be made in order to enhance reutilization projects. (Dry
ash is more easily utilized in secondary processes). All sanitary wastewater
effluent from plant and township would be treated to conform with regulatory
standards and the effluent would be reused to the extent possible. Extensive
afforestation has been undertaken at RhSTPP under Stage I with 700,000 trees
established. The afforestation program would be continued under Stage II
development.
1.20      Rehabilitation and Community Develooment, Stage II:  A socio-
economic study determined 64 land owners and 3 landless families would be
affected/displaced due to land acquisition for the Stage II ash pond. A
Resettlement Action Plan (RAP) for the affected families is being developed in
an ongoing consultation process with the affected parties and local
authorities. The RAP would be based on the latest R&R policy of NTPC and
prepared in consultation with the World Bank.
1.21      The Coal Mine (Dudhichua Stage II) MOEP clearance stipulations
Included phased reclamation of the open cast mine. Currently, 58 hectares of
the mine have been reclaimed. The clearance document also stipulates that land
oustees (87 families) will be rehabilitated according to G0? guidelines as



- 93 -
Annex 3.8
Page 5 of 6
conveyed to NCL.
1.22      Institutional Needs:  As part of the LAP, NTPC will further review
the adequacy of its environmental organization. NTPC will seek assistance of
consultants to strengthen its capabilities in data management, environmental
audits, energy conservation measures, and implementation of mitigation
measures in specific environmental areas. In addition to studies on specified
areas, the expertise of the consultants will be used to formulate pro-active
corporate targets and guidelines for operations and design.
Summary of the EAS for Vindhyachal II
1.23      The Projects The NTPC project will add an additional 1,000 MK
generating capacity as Stage II of the Vindhyachal Superthermbl Power Project
(VSTPP). The associated transmission lines for the project will be
constructed by Power Grid Corporation of India (POCI). The coal mine will be
exploited by Northern Coalfields Ltd. (NCL). All environmental clearances have
been obtained. Since construction of the GBPS reservoir in the 1960s, the
area has undergone large scale industrialization with exploitation of a large
coal deposit, development of coal fired power plants, several chemical
industries, and a cement factory, located about 30 kilometers to the north.
1.24      Project History  Resettlement and Rehabilitation, Stage Is The land
for VSTPP Stage I was acquired through the state government, and 2011
families were affected or displaced. NTPC initiated rehabilitation measures.
A socioeconomic study will be undertaken to ascertain the present economic
status of families affected due to Phase I of the VSTPP project. Based on the
findings of this study, self employment programs through establishment of
village cooperatives would be undertaken with active association of NTPC and
the state government. During development of Dudhichua Hine Stage I, 63
families were resettled and rehabilitated . NCL also initiated community
development activities. Bank supervision missions have confirmed that there
are no oustanding R&R issues with respect to the Stage I mining development.
1.25      Resettlement and Rehabilitation, Stage II   As per the socio-
economic study undertaken by Rewa University, 44 landed, 33 landless and 56
homestead families would be affected due to land acquisition for the Stage II
ash pond. A Resettlement Action Plan for the affected families due to land
acquisition for the ash disposal area for Stage II is being developed in an
ongoing consultation process with the affected parties and local authorities.
The Rehabilitation Action Plan would be based on the latest RIR policy of NTPC
and prepared in consultation with the World Bank. The clearance document for
Dudhichua Nine Stage II stipulates that PAP (estimated at 87 families) will be
rehabilitated according to GOl guidelines as conveyed to NCL. No homesteads
will be acquired for the construction of transmission line substations.
1.26      Environmental Baseline Data.  Studies have revealed contamination
of the reservoir, it's sediments, fish and food crops. Contaminants include
heavy metals, pesticides and other toxic chemicals. The reservoir exhibits
thermal stratification and blue-green algae blooms, which exacerbate dissolved
oxygen depletion in the lower strata. Air quality in the area is generally



- 94 -
Annex 3.8
Page 6 of 6
good, with the exception of wind blown dust.
1.27      VSTPP Stase II Environmental Controls:  Particulate emissions from
the stacks vill be controlled through high efficiency electrostatic
precipitators. The units will be designed for 100 milligram per cubic meter
particulate emissions from the stack after controls. Tall stacks (275 m) will
be used for vider dispersal of atmospheric emissions. A closed cycle cooling
system will be used. Ash generated through the combustion of coal will be
pumped to the ash disposal area as slurry. The decanted water will be
recirculated. low-down from the ash pond slurry water recycling system will
be treated prior to discharge. The ash pond will be provided with impervious
lining in order to prevent leachate coratamination of groundwater.   Provision
for collection of dry flyash will also be made. Dry ash is more easily
utilized in secondary processes. Sanitary effluent from plant and township is
being treated in a sewage treatment plant built in Stage I.
1.28      The Coal Mine (Dudhichua Stase II)   Among the stipulations
included in the MOZF clearance were a phased reclamation of the open cast
mine. Currently, 58 hectares of the mine have been reclaimed.
1.29      Institutional Needs: As part of the ZAP, NTPC will further review
the adequacy of its environmental organization. NTPC will seek assistance of
consultants to strengthen its capabilities in data management, environmental
audits, energy conservation measures, and Implementation of mitigation
measures in specific envi.ronmental areas. In addition to studies on specified
areas, the expertise of the consultants will be used to formulate pro-active
corporate targets and guidelines for operations and design.

INDIA
NTPC POWER GENERATION PROJECT
Bank Supervision Plan
Implementation Review by the Bank
1.        The implementation review of this project would be undertaken along
with the Bank's ongoing projects with NTPC. It is acknowledged that the
proposed time-slice operation which also Includes many enviromental
strengthening actions, would require substantially more Bank staff resources
than a conventional Bank project for the construction of thermal power plants.
The key issues that would be focussed upon ares (a) periodic reviews of NTPC's
investment programs (b) support for NTPC's joint ventures with private
companies; (c) monitoring of compliance with institutional, environmental and
financial covenants; (d) close monitoring of the various consultancy studies
for strengthening NTPC's environmental management and R&R management
capabilities; le) monitoring of the implementation of the power plants funded
under the proposed loan and EAP; (f) active follow up on the R&R programs; and
(g) active follow up on prompt procurement decisions. Bank missions would
particularly assist 001 and NTPC in their efforts to: (i) have NTPC operate in
a more commercial environment; (ii) mitigate the impact of NTPC's power plants
on the environment; and, (iii) implement the R&R programs in a manner fair to
all parties. Implementation review of the project by Bank staff would require
expertise in power engineering, economic and financial analysis,
environmental engineering and R&R. Two implementation review missions
annually for a period of five years are foreseen for adequate supervision of
this project. The total staff input is estimated at an aggregate of 104
staff-weeks, classified as in the following: (a) power engineering -- 35
staff-weeks; (b) economics --  14 staff-weeks; (c) financial analysis and
institutional development -- 28 staff-weeks; id) environmental engineering --
12 staff-weeks; and, (e) Resettlement and Rehabilitation -- 15 staff-weeks.
The Bank supervision plan is attached in the end of this section.

ANNEX 3.0

Quarterly Progress Reports
2.        Monitoring and Reporting bv NTPC.  Under ongoing Bank financed
projects NTPC is required to prepare quarterly reports covering the work of
consultants, procurement, physical progress, project costs, disbursements and
administrative aspects of the project. NTPC's reports have been found to be
too succinct not providing enough information for an efficient project
implementation monitoring and review. During negotiations agreement would be
sought that the scope of the report would be expanded to: (a) cover NTPC's
corporate performance and progress in institutional development; and (b) key
quantitative measurqs of project performance, covering procurement, work of
suppliers, contractors and consultants, physical progress, costs,
disbursements, results of environmental monitoring, and administrative aspects
of the projects funded under the ongoing loans and the proposed loan. NTPC
would begin submitting the quarterly reports under the new format starting
with the quarter in which the loan is signed. The progress reports will be
sent to the Bank within four weeks of the conclusion of the reporting period.
NTPC will also furnish annual financial and administrative reports.
Project Management
3.        NTPC's project management structure involves considerable inputs
from NTPC's staff in the regional offices. Day-to-day implementation is
largely undertaken at the regions; with headquarter's support for design,
procurement, contracting and financial operations. The Corporate Planning
Group (CGG) has been established under Director(Tecbnical) at corporate
headquarters. Site supervisors at each project location report through the
field organization to the General Managers of their respective site. The
Project General Managers chair monthly review meetings attended by concerned
project staff and senior executives of concerned headquarter departments to
plan and review progress and authorize payments to suppliers and contractors.
NTPC management receives monthly progress reports and reviews exceptions at
each project in detail in quarterly Management Committee meetings. Additional
management-level meetings are also convened at short notice when needed to
resolve urgent issues in project implementation. NTPC is currently
introducing computerized project management systems to help schedules and
monitor project implementation and facilitate comprehensive and timely
progress reporting, critical in NTPC's centralized project management
philosophy.

Income Statement
REENUES
1.1       Revenues.  NTPC's projected power sales are not derived, as occur
in most power utilities, from demand projections for a specific market. Since
NTPC's investment programme is the result of decisions, at the central level,
on how the additional generation required to serve the demand projected for
each region in the country is going to be shared among the States and the
Center, NTPC's projected sales are the summation of the power expected to be
generated and sold from each plant. Projected sales are the summation of
operating costs (O&, interest chargeable to operations, interest on working
capital, depreciation, fuel cost) and retuzn on equity. For ongoing projects
the rate of return on equity is assumed as 122 and for new projects, it is
162. For ongoing projects, about 502 of total cost is being financed from GOI
equity or NTPC's own resources.
1.2       Auxiliary Consumption.  Projected as 102 of generation for 2001210
KW units, 32 for combined cycle and gas/steam units and 72 for 500 KW units.
1.3       Electricity Duty.  It is levied by some State Governments of the
Western Region and collected on their behalf by NTPC. It is calculated as 3
paise/kwh.
1.4       Other Income. Includes interest received on short-term deposits,
rental charges for equipment, consulting and management fees, and revenues
from miscellaneous transactions. It is projected as 1X of the electricity
sales.



- 105 -
ANNEX 4.3
Page 2 of 3
EXPENSES
1.5       Fuel Cost.  Calculated as follows.
(a) The base cost of fuel is computed for energy sent out from NTPC's
busbars at its stations. The following elements are included in
the computations
(i)  station heat rate;
(it) specific fuel consumptions
(iii) gross calorific value of coal, oil and gas:
(iv) price of coaligas as delivered; and
(v)  price of oil as delivered.
(b) The base cost is subject to annual fuel price adjustments based oan
local Inflation rates.
1.6       Operation and Maintenance CO&M).  Includes employees cost (221),
repairs and maintenance (332), and administration and others (322). Total O&M
cost is projected as follows:
200/210 MW          Re. 4001kw/year plus 10 increase each year
500 MW              Re. 3001kw/year plus 10  increase each year
Gas Projects        Rs. 240/kw/year plus 10  increase each year
1.7       Depreciation.  Depreciation is calculated at a rate of 4.752 per
annum for thermal (coal) generation plants, and 8.242 for gas based plants.
1.8       Other Expenses. Represents deferred expenses expenditures incurred
In issuing bonds and rebates to customers. It Is projected as the sumuation
oft 1S of total operating revenues plus 22 of bonds issued during the year.
1.9       Interest for the Year.  Represents interest applicable to the
sources of borrowing calculated as follows for new loanss
IBRD                      92 repayment after 5 years in 15 annual
equal installment
ADB                       10? repayment same terms as IBRD
Export Credit             13? repayment after 4 years in 8 annual
equal installment
Bonds                     17? bullet repayment after 7 years
Bilateral Donors          17Z repayment after 5 years in 15 annual
equal installment
Interest on Working       18?
Capital

BALANCE SHEES
1.10      Work in Progress.  Calculated as the balance between additions to
VIP for the year based on estimated project  implementation schedule, and
transfer to fixed assets at the end of the fiscal year of completed projects.
1.11      Cash.  Projected as balancing figure from Sources and App'ication
of Funds.
1.12      Receivables.  The receivable level assumed during the projection
period (except FY1993-94, FY1994-95) is equivalent to the last two months'
outstanding of the (which is 75 days outstanding - based on yearly average).
The receivable at the end of FY1993-94 and M1994-95 is assumed as 105 days
and 90 days, respectively, because of the amounts which remained to be paid
through Central Appropriations.
1.13      Loans and Advances.  Projected as 5? of revenue plus 102 of
investment during the projection period.
1.14      Inventories.  Projected as 20 days (5.5?) fuel cost, two months'
(16.7?) 05M, 6.0? (3.5? for the years 1993-94) total fixed assets during the
year for the 8th plan period. For the remaining years percentage of total
fixed assets is assumed as 5.00?.
1.15      Other Current Assets.  Projected as 30X increase over the previous
year.
1.16      Current Liabilities.  Projected as 60 days' OM cost plus 30 days'
fuel cost mlus 114 of interest chargeable to revenue plus 20? to 27? of
investment during the year. For the years 1993-94 and 1994-95 the percentage
of investment is assumed as 40?.

INDIA                            ANNEX 4.4
Page 1 of 3
NTPC Power Generation ProJect
NTPC Medium and Long-Term Financial Strategy Study
Terms of Reference
I. ObJectives
1.1       With the adoption of the time-slice approach for the financing of its
expansion needs, NTPC would be faced with the following fundamental financial
planning and strategic tasks:
(a) Formulation of long-term financial plans, policies and strategies
corresponding to its long-term corporate expansion objectives
(b) Formulation of short-to-medium-term strategies and policies for
financing sequential investment time-slices; and
(c)  Ensuring the necessary coherence and compatibility of its  short-to-
medium and medium-to-long-term financial policies and strategies;
iv) Introduction of a dynamic resource mobilization concept into NTPC's
financial strategies and policies; and
(d) Formulation and implementation of corresponding organizational and
personnel changes in NTPC's Finance Department.
II. The Scope of Work
1.2       It is envisaged that NTPC's financial strategy would be studied as a
series of long-term (at least 10-year) alternatives, customarily tested for
sensitivity.
(a) The Base Case
The physical expansion envisaged by the plan for 1993/4 - 199718
should be taken as the base case for which an optimum (optimum meaning
primarily least risk, not necessarily least cost) financial strategy,
based on an agreed optimum debt/equity structure and complemented by
a feasible optimum mix of locally and externally mobilized resources,
should be recommended.
(b) Alternative Cases
Following the formulation of the base case strategy, alternative
financial strategies should also be analyzeds
Ci) Maximum expansion case, assuming that all major works, currently
under preparation by NTPC would be carried out;



- 108 -
ANNEX 4.4
Page 2 of 3
(ii) Variant cases, e.g. the base case + 20X., the maximum case - 202
etc.
(c) The DRnamic Case
(i)  Based on the analysis of the base case, the maximum case and the
alternative cases, a dynamic (optimum) case financial strategy
should be developed. The latter implies a strategy adjustable
according tot ti) changing availability of domestic & external
financing;
(ii) (ii) constraints in internal resource mobilization because
Zactors like current tariff policies level of bill collection
etc.; (iii) possible broadening of NTPC's equity base through
partial divestiture, dilution of public ownership by raising
additional private equity etc.
1.3       Presently, the bulk of NTPC's major expansion works is undertaken only
once the requisite, project-specific, external resources have been contracted -
i.e. NTPC's expansion is financed on the basis of a 'static' resource mix. In
the future, given anticipated broad changes in India's financial environment,
ranging from the introduction of Rupee convertibility to the opening of domestic
capital market, NTPC will have to consider securing a steady flow of finance from
the mix of available local and foreign sources, rather than arranging 'static'
financing packages for individual investment activities.
III. Main Policy Facets to be Analyzed
1.4       The  analysis of the above mentioned alternatives will have  to
encompass at least the following five main facets of NTPC's overall financial
policies:
(a) The internal resource mobilization policy
(b) NTPC's equity base expansion policy (re. options to raise additional
private andlor public equity, existing equity dilution options etc.
options to raise foreign equity);
(c) The finacial asset and liability management policy (re. analysis of
options available to NTPC with particular emphasis on interest rate
trends and foreign exchange risks etc.; development of procedures for
optimum funding mix determination over a given time horizon, such as
a time-slice or a five-year plan period etc.)
ld) The resource mobilization policy (i.e. local and foreign borrowing
policy). A very detailed analysis is envisaged here, covering:
-   local money and capital markets;
- foreign money and capital markets (including syndicated
borrowings and issues of securities including securities
convertible into equity);



109 -
ANS= 4.4
page 3 of 3
- exportisupplier credit marketst
- official development assistance.
(e) Optimization of liluidity mannaement
Time-and duration-specific options under 1.4 above should be examined
under various NTPC expansion scenarios.
IV.       The Implementation Schedule
1.5       As a part of the study. an implementation schedule should be prepated
for operationali-ing the dynamic financial strategy in NTPC (including the
recommendations for organizational and policy changes as well as resulting
personnel requirements).
Review of Recommendations
1.6       Upon the completion of the study, the Bank and WMPC will jointly
review the study recomendations and their prospective Implementation not later
than September 30, 1994. During the review. MPC will exchange views with the
Bank at appropriate intervals.

ANNEX 5.1
Page 1 of 3
INDIA
NTPC POWER GENERATION PROJECT
Economic Analysis
1.1       The analysis focuses on NTPC'8 core investment program, which is
supported in part by the proposed Bank loan. The two generation projects which
meet the selection criteria for Bank financing and are ready for implementation
under the proposed loan, Vindhyachal and Rihand 2x5OO KW coal-fired power station
extensions, form an integral part of this core investment program.
1.2       Economic Viability of NTPC's Investment Program.  The economic rate
of return (ERR) was calculated on the basis of the incremental cost and benefit
streams associated with the 1993-2000 time-slice of NTPC's investment program.
The time-slice period covers investments supported under the proposed project and
the Bank's ongoing generation projects with NTPC.
1.3       Costs.  The investment plan is discussed in paras 2.24-2.27 of the
main text and detailed listing of its components is given in Annex 2.6. Projects
shown in Annex 2.6 to be completed during the time-slice period were taken as the
time-slice investment proram. Financial costs of that program were converted to
economic terms by excluding taxes and duties and by applying a standard
conversion factor (SCP) of 0.8 to the residual local costs. The resulting total
time-slice investments are shown in Table 5.1. Economic cost of NTPC's main fuel
(local coal) was updated from the Bank's study of the Long Term Issues in the
Power Sector, gas was priced at fuel oil parity. The prices NTPC pays for its
coal supplies are generally slightly higher than the estimated economic costs,
the price of gas is about 75Z of fuel oil parity, falling behind the targeted
fuel oil parity due to recent substantial depreciation of the Rupee.
1.4       Also shown in Table 5.1 are NTPC's incremental (in excess of 1993,
base year of the analysis) operations and maintenance (O&M) costs, taken from
NTPC's projected financial statements given in Annex 4.2 and converted to
economic terms by excluding taxes and duties and by applying SC? to the residual
local costs. O& costs of the last year of the time-slice investment period were
kept constant in real terms for the operating period of time-slice investments.
1.5       Benefits.  For the purpose of ERR calculations, NTPC's incremental
tariff revenue was used as a proxy for the economic benefits of its investment
program and operations.  NTPC's tariffs are discussed in paras 2.21-2.23 in the
main text, billing and collection in paras. 4.9-4.10. NTPC's assets are not
revalued for tariff setting purposes, hence the fixed cost part of NTPC's two-
part tariff for each station declines in real terms over time, in line with
inflation. Incremental revenue of the last year of the 1993-2000 time-slice
investment period was, however, kept constant in real terms for the
2001-2030 operating period of time-slice investmentst it is not reasonable to
assume that the economlc value of electricity would decline. On the contrary,
tariff revenue is regarded to be the minimum measure of the actual benefits as
tariff revenue reflects only a portion of the total beneflts of Incremental power
supply, given India's chronic shortage of electricity. The ERR of the program



- 111 -
ANNEX 5.1
Page 2 of 3
is nevertheless satisfactory at about 14.7Z with this conservative revenue-based
benefit valuation. The net present value of the program at 12? discount rate is
about Rs 16.9 billion.
1.6       Robustness of the Program. NTPC's time-slice ERR is not significantly
affected by changes in the costs of the investment program and in the
implementation schedules of its individual components. This is due to NTPC's
ability under its tariff setting principles to fully pass on to its clients its
actual investment and fuel costs and these account for the major part of NTPC's
total costs.   The tariff includes a provision for recovering operating and
maintenance (O&M) costs using normative tariff parameters, i.e. not on the basis
of actual costs. The impact of adverse changes from the most critical normative
values was examined in sensitivity analysis.   A 102 increase in heat rate
(reduction in efficiency) brought the ERR down to 13.42; a 10? reduction in plant
load factor (PLF) reduced ERR to 12.3Z. Should both of these adverse changes
take place simultaneously, i.e. reduced generation at lower efficiency, the ERR
is reduced further to 11.0X. It should be noted that NTPC may also be able to
exceed the normative performance (hear rate, availability etc.) targets, in which
case the ERRs would correspondingly increase from the base case ERR. Given
India's power shortages, it is likely that NTPC will have the opportunity to
generate well above the normative annual generation targets and, assuming its
plants perform, will be able to earn returns exceeding the normative 162 return
on equity (in the base case of the analysis).
1.7       NTPC's investment program is constrained by the available financing,
not by demand for NTPC-generated electricity.   Power supply is projected to
constrain electricity consumption in India well beyond the year 2000 and the risk
for lower than projected generation due to low demand is marginal.   A 101
reduction in demand would reduce the ERR to 14.1?. In the case of NTPC, its
"demand* forecast Is essentially a supply forecast (projected output of the
generating stations) and will be lower than projected only in case the supply
does not materialize, i.e. in case the stations do not generate as much as
projected, e.g. due to insufficient fuel supply or lower plant availability.
That scenario was tested in the sensitivity analysis by reducing the PLF by 10Z,
as discussed above. The ERR decreases less in the reduced demand case than in
the case of lower generation, as under the tariff setting principles, if NTPC is
required to back down due to low demand, it is credited for the resulting
reduction in generation (deemed generation) for the fixed-cost portion of the
two-part tariff - hence the revenues decline less than when the generation is
reduced due to its own performance.
1.8       The above revenue based analysis reflects only a portion of the total
benefits of NTPC's operations and still yields a satisfactory ERR of about 14.7X
- hence further ERR calculations are not required to establish the viability of
the program.
